<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background:transparent;text-align:left;font-weight:normal;">4 currencies</div>
<ul class="NavContent" style="list-style: none none; margin-left: 0; text-align: left; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> &#160;<span style="font-size:85%;">(ARS)</span>&#160; <a href="/wiki/Argentine_peso" title="Argentine peso">Peso</a>
  </li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> &#160;<span style="font-size:85%;">(BRL)</span>&#160; <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">Real</a>
  </li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> &#160;<span style="font-size:85%;">(PYG)</span>&#160; <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_guaran%C3%AD" title="Paraguayan guaraní">Guaraní</a>
  </li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"> &#160;<span style="font-size:85%;">(UYU)</span>&#160; <a href="/wiki/Uruguayan_peso" title="Uruguayan peso">Peso</a>
 </li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em;">
<li value="1"><a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">Pardo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">Mestizo</a>, etc.</li><li value="2">Considering Mercosur as a single entity.</li><li value="3"><i><a href="/wiki/Pro_tempore" title="Pro tempore">Pro tempore</a></i>.<span style="font-size: 120%;"><sup id="cite_ref-reuters.com_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></span></li>
</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Mercosur</b> (in Spanish), <b>Mercosul</b> (in Portuguese), or <b>Ñemby Ñemuha</b> (in <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guarani</a>), officially <b>Southern Common Market</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South American</a> <a href="/wiki/Trade_bloc" title="Trade bloc">trade bloc</a> established by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Treaty of Asunción">Treaty of Asunción</a> in 1991 and <a href="/wiki/Protocol_of_Ouro_Preto" title="Protocol of Ouro Preto">Protocol of Ouro Preto</a> in 1994. Its full members are <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>. <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> is a full member but has been suspended since December 1, 2016. Associate countries are  <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Observer_status" title="Observer status">Observer countries</a> are <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mercosur's purpose is to promote <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a> and the fluid movement of goods, people, and currency. Since its foundation, Mercosur's functions have been updated and amended many times; it currently confines itself to a <a href="/wiki/Customs_union" title="Customs union">customs union</a>, in which there is free intra-zone trade and a common trade policy between member countries. The official languages are Spanish, Portuguese, and Guarani.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mercosur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding">Founding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mercosur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Founding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sede_del_Mercosur_-_Montevideo,_Uruguay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Sede_del_Mercosur_-_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.jpg/220px-Sede_del_Mercosur_-_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Sede_del_Mercosur_-_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.jpg/330px-Sede_del_Mercosur_-_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Sede_del_Mercosur_-_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.jpg/440px-Sede_del_Mercosur_-_Montevideo%2C_Uruguay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1832" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sede_del_Mercosur_-_Montevideo,_Uruguay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/w/index.php?title=Headquarters_of_Mercosur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Headquarters of Mercosur (page does not exist)">Headquarters of Mercosur</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edificio_Mercosur" class="extiw" title="es:Edificio Mercosur">es</a>&#93;</span>, Montevideo, Uruguay.</div></div></div>
<p>Mercosur was established in 1991 by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Treaty of Asunción">Treaty of Asunción</a>, which was later amended and updated by the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Ouro_Preto" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Ouro Preto">Treaty of Ouro Preto</a>.
Mercosur originated in 1988, when presidents <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Alfons%C3%ADn" title="Raúl Alfonsín">Raúl Alfonsín</a> of Argentina and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Sarney" title="José Sarney">José Sarney</a> of Brazil signed the <i>Argentina-Brazil Integration and Economics Cooperation Program</i> or <b>PICE</b> (Portuguese: Programa de Integração e Cooperação Econômica Argentina-Brasil, Spanish: Programa de Integración y Cooperación Económica Argentina-Brasil).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The protocol Number 20 of the program also proposed the <a href="/wiki/Gaucho_(currency)" title="Gaucho (currency)">Gaucho</a> as a currency for regional trade.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The founding of the <a href="/wiki/Mercosur_Parliament" title="Mercosur Parliament">Mercosur Parliament</a> was agreed upon at the December 2004 presidential summit. Up to 2010 it was planned to have 18 representatives from each country, regardless of population.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Memberships_and_suspensions">Memberships and suspensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mercosur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Memberships and suspensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Suspension_of_Paraguay">Suspension of Paraguay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mercosur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Suspension of Paraguay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Izamiento.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Izamiento.jpg/220px-Izamiento.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="299" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Izamiento.jpg/330px-Izamiento.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Izamiento.jpg/440px-Izamiento.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2182" data-file-height="2966" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Izamiento.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>First lifting headquarters of Mercosur in Montevideo (2001).</div></div></div>
<p>After suspending Paraguay in 2012, the presidents of the Mercosur countries (Argentina, Brazil, Uruguay, and Venezuela) said in July 2013 that they would lift the suspension after the inauguration of Paraguay's newly elected President, <a href="/wiki/Horacio_Cartes" title="Horacio Cartes">Horacio Cartes</a>, on 15 August 2013. However, Paraguay said it would not return to the Mercosur fold as long as Venezuela held its rotating presidency. Venezuela held Mercosur's rotating presidency until July 2014. Paraguay has objected to Venezuela's inclusion in the trading bloc, and says that a new member can only be included after a unanimous vote and argues that such a vote should not have been held while Paraguay was suspended.<sup id="cite_ref-President_Cartes_sworn_in_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-President_Cartes_sworn_in-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Eladio_Loizaga" title="Eladio Loizaga">Eladio Loizaga</a> said he would rather deal with Paraguay's neighbours individually at first. "We have pending issues with Argentina, with Uruguay; we have to recompose all that," he said. "Mercosur will be later because our priority are &#32;&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>&#93; the bilateral relations," he added.<sup id="cite_ref-President_Cartes_sworn_in_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-President_Cartes_sworn_in-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bolivian_membership_status">Bolivian membership status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mercosur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Bolivian membership status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 7 December 2012, Bolivian President <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> signed a protocol aimed at accession to full membership of the block.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Such a proposal requires review and possible legislative approval.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> On July 7 of 2015, the heads of Mercosur having decided to accept Bolivia's request to become a full member country, Bolivian president Evo Morales signed the Brasilia protocol. This acted as Bolivia's full membership to the Mercosur.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Suspension_of_Venezuela">Suspension of Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mercosur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Suspension of Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Conferencia-_%22Integraci%C3%B3n_Latinoamericana_y_Mercosur%22_(7402119210).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Conferencia-_%22Integraci%C3%B3n_Latinoamericana_y_Mercosur%22_%287402119210%29.jpg/220px-Conferencia-_%22Integraci%C3%B3n_Latinoamericana_y_Mercosur%22_%287402119210%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Conferencia-_%22Integraci%C3%B3n_Latinoamericana_y_Mercosur%22_%287402119210%29.jpg/330px-Conferencia-_%22Integraci%C3%B3n_Latinoamericana_y_Mercosur%22_%287402119210%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Conferencia-_%22Integraci%C3%B3n_Latinoamericana_y_Mercosur%22_%287402119210%29.jpg/440px-Conferencia-_%22Integraci%C3%B3n_Latinoamericana_y_Mercosur%22_%287402119210%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Conferencia-_%22Integraci%C3%B3n_Latinoamericana_y_Mercosur%22_(7402119210).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Conference of Latin-American Integration</div></div></div>
<p>In August 2016, the presidents of Brazil, Argentina, and Paraguay, while present in Rio de Janeiro for the Olympic Games, met to discuss suspending Venezuela from Mercosur. The three countries were in doubt about whether Venezuela was complying with the union's requirements for full membership, citing <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_violations" class="mw-redirect" title="Human rights violations">human rights violations</a> among other issues.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>  In fact, Venezuela was rejected from assuming the presidency of Mercosur by those three countries, prompting a dispute that continued to the end of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 November 2016, Paraguayan Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Eladio_Loizaga" title="Eladio Loizaga">Eladio Loizaga</a> announced that Venezuela would be suspended in December 2016 after the nation was given a three-month period to reform its laws to abide to Mercosur requirements, with Mercosur noting that "rules governing trade, politics, democracy and human rights" needed to be overhauled in Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> On 1 December 2016, Venezuela was suspended from Mercosur.<sup id="cite_ref-APvenSUS_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APvenSUS-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Member_states">Member states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mercosur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Member states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_Mercosur" title="Member states of Mercosur">Member states of Mercosur</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mercosur.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Mercosur.png/220px-Mercosur.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9a/Mercosur.png 1.5x" data-file-width="330" data-file-height="410" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mercosur.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dark blue: Full members<br />Grey blue: Associated members<br />Blue: Observer members</div></div></div>
<p>Mercosur is composed of 5 <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign</a> member states: Argentina; Brazil; Paraguay; Uruguay and Venezuela (suspended since December, 2016); and a state in process of incorporation, Bolivia (since July 17, 2015)<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Fernando_Lugo" title="Impeachment of Fernando Lugo">impeachment of President Fernando Lugo</a> by the Paraguayan Senate, this country was suspended from Mercosur, and the admittance of Venezuela as a full member became effective on 31 July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters.com_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Venezuela had four years to fully adapt to the trade bloc regulations<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and failed to do so, with the nation being suspended from Mercosur on 1 December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-APvenSUS_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APvenSUS-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Directly subordinated to the Common Market Group, the Work Subgroups draw up the minutes of the decisions to submit for the consideration of the Council, and study specific Mercosur concerns. The work subgroups are: 
</p>
<ul><li>Commercial matters</li>
<li>Customs matters</li>
<li>Technical standards</li>
<li>Tax and monetary policies relating to trade</li>
<li>Land transport</li>
<li>Sea transport</li>
<li>Industrial and technology policies</li>
<li>Agricultural policy</li>
<li>Energy policy</li>
<li>Coordination of macroeconomic policies</li>
<li>Labor, employment and social security matters</li></ul>
<p>Work subgroups are held quarterly, alternating in every member state, in alphabetical order, or at the Common Market Group Administrative Office. Activities are carried out by the Work Subgroups in two stages: preparatory and conclusive. In the preparatory stage, members of the Work Subgroups may request the participation of representatives from the private sector of each member state. The decision-making stage is reserved exclusively for official representatives of the member states. The delegations of representatives from the private sector in the preparatory stage of the Work Subgroup activities will have a maximum of three representatives for each member state directly involved in any of the stages of the production, distribution or consumption process for the products that fall within the scope of the subgroup's activities.,
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mercosur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The territory of Mercosur consists of the combined territories of six of the 12 countries of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and their population. Including the overseas territories of member states, Mercosur experiences most <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">types of climate</a> from <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">Antarctic</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a>, rendering meteorological averages for Mercosur as a whole meaningless. The majority of the population lives in areas with a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical climate</a> (Uruguay, Southern Paraguay, Northeastern Argentina and Southern and Southeastern Brazil), or a tropical climate (Venezuela and Northeastern Brazil).
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1008px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Iguazu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Panorama_7.jpg" class="image" title="Iguazu Falls on the border between Argentina and Brazil is an area with subtropical climate and are one of the New Seven World Natural Wonders."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Iguazu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Panorama_7.jpg/1000px-Iguazu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Panorama_7.jpg" decoding="async" width="1000" height="216" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Iguazu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Panorama_7.jpg/1500px-Iguazu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Panorama_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Iguazu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Panorama_7.jpg/2000px-Iguazu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Panorama_7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5122" data-file-height="1106" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iguazu_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Panorama_7.jpg" title="File:Iguazu Décembre 2007 - Panorama 7.jpg"> </a></div><center><a href="/wiki/Iguazu_Falls" title="Iguazu Falls">Iguazu Falls</a> on the border between Argentina and Brazil is an area with <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical climate</a> and are one of the <a href="/wiki/New7Wonders_of_Nature" title="New7Wonders of Nature">New Seven World Natural Wonders</a>.</center></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mercosur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="wikitable">

<p>The region is highly urbanized, and the largest cities in Mercosur are the <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global cities</a> <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>. The white population is the majority in Argentina and Uruguay and represents around half the population in Brazil. Mestizos form the majority population in Paraguay.<sup id="cite_ref-bar_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bar-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Almost all Mercosur nations have significant Native American populations, especially in Paraguay (Guaraní is a national language in the country along with Spanish, and almost all Paraguayans have Guaraní genetic ancestry), Argentina (especially in the country's North-Western, Northern, and Southern provinces), Brazil (in the Northern Amazonian states of the nation, where Native American tribes have vast reservation lands).
</p><p>Along with Paraguay (where it is one of two official languages), sectors of Argentina (Corrientes) speak Guaraní. However, the Mercosur does not provide all, or even most, services in Guaraní. The official website and almost all official summits are only held in Spanish and Portuguese.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Merchandise_trade">Merchandise trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mercosur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Merchandise trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Intra-Mercosur merchandise trade (excluding Venezuela) grew from US$10 billion at the inception of the trade bloc in 1991,<sup id="cite_ref-ege_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ege-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> to US$88 billion in 2010; Brazil and Argentina each accounted for 43% of this total.<sup id="cite_ref-dg_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dg-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The trade balance within the bloc has historically been tilted toward Brazil,<sup id="cite_ref-ege_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ege-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> which recorded an intra-Mercosur balance of over US$5 billion in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-dg_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dg-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Trade within Mercosur amounted to only 16% of the four countries' total merchandise trade in 2010, however; trade with the European Union (20%), China (14%), and the United States (11%) was of comparable importance.<sup id="cite_ref-dg_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dg-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Exports from the bloc are highly diversified, and include a variety of agricultural, industrial, and energy goods. Merchandise trade with the rest of the world in 2010 resulted in a surplus for Mercosur of nearly US$7 billion; <a href="/wiki/Trade_in_services" title="Trade in services">trade in services</a>, however, was in deficit by over US$28 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-dg_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dg-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The EU and China maintained a nearly balanced merchandise trade with Mercosur in 2010, while the United States reaped a surplus of over US$14 billion; Mercosur, in turn, earned significant surpluses (over US$4 billion each in 2010) in its trade with Chile and Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-dg_28-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dg-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The latter became a full member in 2012.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mercosur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
